Sequel to the Nanning and Hubei Collision

Sailing to Tortoise Mountain, a Thick Fog Suddenly Arises

Ordered to Throw Soybean Cakes, the Bow of the Ship Floats

The Nanning vessel of the British Swire Company collided with the Hubei vessel of our company near Xiamen. Both vessels were severely damaged, with the Nanning suffering even greater losses. A brief account has been published in the previous newspaper. Last night, the Hubei vessel arrived in Shanghai. The reporter went to various parties to investigate the circumstances of the accident, as follows:

Collision in the Fog

The Nanning vessel of the Swire Company operates on the Niuzhuang, Dalian, Shantou, and Xiamen route. This time, the vessel was specially dispatched to transport a large batch of soybean cakes from Yingkou to South China. On April 30th, around 9:00 AM, when the ship was nearly one hundred nautical miles from Xiamen, at a place called Tortoise Mountain, a thick fog suddenly arose on the sea, making it impossible to see even a short distance away. The Nanning vessel continued to sail in the fog. At this time, the Hubei vessel was also sailing from Hong Kong to Shanghai with goods. It was also sailing to Tortoise Mountain. In the fog, the Nanning and Hubei were on a straight line and were obscured by the fog. Neither vessel saw each other until they were close. The Nanning and Hubei tried to avoid each other, but it was too late, and the two vessels collided.

Both Ships Damaged

The Hubei and Nanning vessels were each sailing. The Nanning vessel was faster and crashed into the Hubei vessel first. The Hubei vessel was unable to avoid it, and the bow was severely damaged. The steel plates around the anchor hole were broken, and the bow was collapsed. Fortunately, the damage was above the waterline, so the rupture was not too severe, and there was no water ingress. The Nanning vessel was hit behind the bow, and the outer hull of the first hold was struck by the Hubei, creating a large hole between the waterlines. The Nanning vessel then heavily　took on seawater, causing a great danger.

Abandoning Huge Cargo

After the Nanning ship's hull was damaged, seeing that seawater had entered the forward hold and the hull was gradually sinking, the situation was extremely critical. In order to remedy the situation, the captain immediately ordered the soybean cakes loaded in the forward hold to be quickly thrown into the sea in order to reduce the load. Eight out of ten of the several hundred tons of soybean cakes in the forward hold were thrown into the sea. The forward hold gradually rose, and the sailors were ordered to pump the water out of the hold, so that the hull could be preserved and not sink. It was truly a great stroke of luck amidst misfortune.

Nanchang Towing and Rescue

When the Nanning was in danger, fortunately the Nanchang vessel of the same company sailed past the Tortoise Mountain sea area. The Nanning flew a　flag for help, and the Nanchang vessel immediately sailed to rescue it. The Nanning vessel was towed to Xiamen. It was originally going to Shantou, but changed course to Xiamen due to the accident. The cargo was first unloaded, and then it will go to Hong Kong for repairs.

Hubei Returns to Shanghai

The Hubei vessel set off first to Shanghai after the fog cleared. Yesterday, it had already entered port. The bow was broken. Yesterday, it was unloading cargo in Pudong, and then it will go to the factory for repairs. The Nanning vessel suffered huge losses this time. The hull and cargo were worth at least 30,000 yuan. The Hubei's losses were also six or seven thousand taels. Fortunately, the accident occurred during the daytime, so no one was injured.

Sequel to the Ship Accident

Waking Lion Enters Dock

The Waking Lion vessel of the Sanbei Company collided with the French postal ship Sphinx on the Lujiazui river surface of the Huangpu River on its way from Shanghai to Haizhou, as reported in this newspaper. The damage to the Waking Lion was at the bow, while the damage to the French vessel was at the stern. After the Waking Lion returned to the Nidu Wharf, the Sanbei Company immediately invited surveyor Mr. Engels to the ship to survey the damage. It was estimated that repairs would cost at least 7,000 taels. Yesterday, the cargo on the ship was transferred to the Fulong vessel to be transported to Haizhou. The Waking Lion was originally going to undergo major repairs. Yesterday, it was towed into the Sanbei Main Factory to begin repairs. It is estimated that it will take one month before it can leave the factory. As for the five sugar barges that were sunk by the Waking Lion, with the loss of more than 300 bags of sugar, the owners of the lost cargo negotiated with Sanbei yesterday for compensation. The Sanbei Company must send a surveyor to investigate before determining the method. As for the damage to the stern of the French postal ship, it was also verified by Engels to be about 3,000 taels in repair costs. However, due to the schedule, it could not stay in Shanghai for long and has already sailed to Japan. As for the question of responsibility for the accident, according to the Waking Lion captain of Sanbei, Weng Jiqing, the collision was unavoidable. According to the French shipowner's report, when turning the ship, the vessel had already hoisted the stop-ship-passing warning ball, but the Waking Lion still moved forward, so the responsibility lies with the Waking Lion.

Minghe Towing and Rescue

After the Minghe vessel ran aground north of Vladivostok, the crew escaped to the summit of Shipai Nuofu Reef to take shelter. Yesterday, the Sanbei Company received a telegram from Vladivostok stating that the Minghe was still aground and had not sunk. The crew and sailors on the mountain had returned to the ship and are waiting for Shanghai to send a vessel to rescue them. The company is waiting for the new Nining Xing to return from Hankou today. After dismantling the radio equipment and installing it on the Fengpu vessel, it will set off to the scene of the accident to rescue the crew and inspect the situation in order to tow the vessel. The Fengpu is scheduled to go to Vladivostok tomorrow.

Daji Repair

The shell of the Daji vessel of the Dada Company, which was bombed, has been towed back to Shanghai. Because the machinery and engine are incomplete, it has been decided to carry out major repairs, which will be undertaken by the Ruian factory. The entire superstructure above the main deck must be rebuilt, which will take three months to complete. The repair cost will be 160,000 taels of silver, and the repair contract has been signed. It is expected to be able to leave the factory and operate within September of this year.

The money will be given to their families when they come to Shanghai to collect it. 2. The nineteen Cantonese crew members Ling Hong, Lin Xiong, Lu Tiao, Ling Ji, Luo Jiewen, Hua Liangyuan, Lin Bing, Tan Yufen, Chen Yu, Liang Bingrong, Lin Jia, Ling Liang, Li Min, Lin Chang, Zhu He, Lin Jing, Xu Jiu, Cai Cheng, etc., will be given 80 yuan each as compensation, in addition to the temporary relief money of 15 yuan each that was previously issued by the French Concession police. 3. Explanation of the Nature of the Qualifying Examination

Designed for Outstanding Young People Who Cannot Afford to Study

The Municipal Qualifying Examination Committee yesterday received instructions from the Examination Yuan, according to the Hunan Qualifying Examination Committee's explanation of the nature of the examination, stating that Article 4 of the Examination Law stipulates that graduates of registered public or private secondary schools or above, or those with equivalent academic qualifications to graduates of secondary schools or above, who have passed the qualifying examination, may take the general examination. Article 5 stipulates that graduates of national or registered public or private colleges or above, or graduates of foreign colleges or above recognized by the Ministry of Education, or those with equivalent academic qualifications to graduates of universities or colleges, who have passed the qualifying examination, may take the higher examination. The higher and general qualifying examinations are purely designed to select outstanding young people who cannot afford to study. All those who have equivalent academic qualifications to higher and general examinations without graduating from a school or graduating from a school not approved by the Ministry of Education may take the qualifying examination. Upon passing the qualifying examination, a certificate will be issued, and they will be qualified to take the higher or general examination.

Crisis in the Foreign Trade of Raw Silk

Lyon Silk Trade Association's Letter of Advice

Hoping for Improvements in Manufacturing Methods

The Lyon Silk Trade Association of France has recently sent letters and telegrams to the Shanghai Raw Silk Exporters Association, stating that "The poor quality of Chinese filature silk has caused great difficulties and dangers in the French market. Silk merchants here will soon seek other sources. It is hoped that there will be improvements in manufacturing methods and strict inspections." It also said, "In this period of economic panic, commodity trade is already extremely difficult. Lax inspections will only create negative results. The quality of raw silk produced in your region is deteriorating.　At a time when various countries are demanding increasingly stricter management methods for raw silk and other silk-producing countries such as Japan and Italy are making great progress, the decline in the quality of Chinese raw silk will have a huge impact, and both your region and our region will suffer. Special attention must be paid to make silk factories aware of the dangers ahead and to make improvements." After receiving the information, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, believing that the matter concerned the future of the silk industry in various countries, invited sericulture experts to a meeting on the 27th of last month for an informal discussion. They all believed that the poor quality of cocoons was due to poor　manufacturing, and the sericulturalists' greed for profit was also an important reason. In addition,　manufacturers failed to reduce the price of inferior cocoons to make them aware, and poor management and labor disputes in silk factories led to affecting raw silk production. It was decided　that all parties should work together to save the situation. On one hand, the bureau will report the dangerous situation of raw silk foreign trade and the decided improvement methods to the Ministry of Industry for reference in improving the national silk industry. It is also heard that the Shanghai Raw Silk Exporters Association also plans to submit a list of all the issues to the Ministry of Industry and request their adoption and implementation.

Appointment of Silk Cocoon Insurance Adjusters

Every time silk factories in this city send staff with funds to the interior to make cocoons, they must insure against fire, water, theft, and other risks with Chinese and foreign insurance companies before. If an accident occurs, the insurance company must appoint a surveyor to assess the value of the damaged goods before compensating according to the discount. This surveyor is only selected unilaterally by the insurance company without seeking the consent of the insured party, which is unfair. Letters have been sent to trade associations requesting collective discussion and relief. Now, the silk factory associations of the three regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai have sent a joint letter to the insurance association requesting that in the future, if an accident occurs, the selected surveyor must obtain the consent of the insured party before being appointed, so as to be fair.

The Municipal Government Assigns Trainees from the Self-Government Training Institute for Internship

The Municipal Government is very cautious in opening the Local Self-Government Training Institute for all facilities. The trainees in the first ordinary class, in addition to receiving direct training for three months to increase their knowledge, must also intern for three months to increase their experience. Now that the trainees have completed their studies, they have been assigned to different internships and have formulated provisional regulations for trainees' internships. The institute is scheduled to convene all trainees for a speech on the afternoon of the 4th of this month.

Cai Zhengya Speaks on Recent Labor Issues in Shanghai

The China Industrial and Commercial Management Association held its seventh luncheon discussion meeting at the Lianhua General Association yesterday afternoon. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Social Bureau, was invited to speak on the various aspects of labor-management cooperation. However, Mr. Pan went to Beijing for the National Assembly and entrusted Mr. Cai Zhengya to attend and deliver a speech on "Recent Labor Issues in Shanghai." Dr. Kong Yongzhi, Chairman of the Board, sent a telegram to the meeting because he could not come to Shanghai on official business. Therefore, the members present elected Mr. Pan Wenan as the chairman. After the meal, the chairman delivered an opening speech, and then Mr. Cai Zhengya stood up to speak. He divided the recent three-year labor situation in Shanghai into labor-management disputes, wages and working hours, and living expenses, and listed statistical figures for comparison and explanation. He said that the labor movement in Shanghai has gradually entered the right track after several years of turmoil and disputes. It is hoped that labor and management will be deeply aware and work together to increase the total amount of the national economy. Then, Honorary Secretary-General Cao Yunxiang spoke on the relationship between scientific management and labor-management issues, and the meeting adjourned at 2:30 PM.

Two Women's Groups Jointly Hold a Labor Issues Research Conference

The Shanghai YWCA and the Shanghai Women's Association believe that female and child labor in modern industry has become a serious issue that should attract the attention of the community. Therefore, they held a labor issues research conference at the YWCA on Nanjing Road for the past three days. Mrs. Chang Ma served as chairman by rotation, and Ms. Deng Yuzhi, secretary of the Labor Department of the National Association of YWCAs, led the discussion. Various charts and graphs were displayed in the meeting place to show the situation of female and child labor in various places. Attendees included people from academic, commercial, medical, and family backgrounds, which was very grand at the time. The main points of the discussion over the past few days are briefly described below. Regarding the comparison of the number of male and female child laborers in Shanghai, working hours, and working conditions, Ms. Deng put forward the following points: 1. Number of workers: According to the Shanghai Municipal Social

Bureau's survey, there are 125,785 female workers (with textile workers accounting for the majority), accounting for 57% of all factory workers in Shanghai, 76,248 male workers, accounting for 34% of the total, and 20,637 child laborers, accounting for 9% of the total. 2. Working hours: According to the survey conducted by the Labor Department of the Shanghai YWCA, more than 22,000 of the more than 30,000 female workers work 11 to 12 hours a day. Most female workers only have two days off per month. Cotton mills work in two shifts, day and night, changing shifts every week. The day shift is from 6:00 AM to 6:00 PM, and the night shift is from 6:00 PM to 6:00 AM. 3. Wages: The average worker earns 6 jiao per day. According to the survey by the Ministry of Industry, workers in the 30 largest cities allocate 82.59% of their wages to food, clothing, and housing, and only 17.41% to education, entertainment, social relations, and illness. 4. The excessive working hours and poor working conditions have many harmful effects on female workers. A. Cutting off fingers, hair, and arms being caught in belts, resulting in permanent disability or immediate death. B. Due to poor air circulation, excessive humidity, and excessive dust, female workers in silk and cotton mills often suffer from lung and throat problems. 5. Affects the health of female workers and hinders the nurturing of strong children and healthy citizens. 6. Child labor under the age of 14 working in factories has the following results: A. They are not educated and grow up to be ignorant citizens. B. Without exercise and rest, they grow up to be unhealthy citizens. C. Child labor wages are too low, affecting adult workers' unemployment. Three major methods are proposed for solving the problem of female and child labor: 1. Employers voluntarily improve working hours and working conditions and run welfare programs. For example, Tiancheng Cotton Mill in Tianjin, the Shanghai Commercial Press, and Yongtai Mingfeng Silk Mill in Wuxi are all pioneers in voluntarily improving the working system, and the results are very good. 2. Workers organize and take collective action to put forward conditions for improvement to employers, but it is believed that effective worker movements must focus on worker education. 3. The government uses legislation to urge factories to improve working conditions, but whether the Factory Law can be implemented depends on the power of public opinion. Attendees all believed that women have a responsibility to promote public opinion on banning child labor and protecting female workers. They also believed that women, standing in the position of consumers, have the ability to improve the lives of female and child workers, but various social forces must be concentrated and unified to produce results. Therefore, it was decided to convene a joint meeting of representatives of women's groups in Shanghai at noon next Monday, May 4, to come up with concrete measures.

The Story of China Donating a Pair of Stone Lions to an American University

Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi, on behalf of the government, donated two stone lions to the University of Missouri. A year ago, the university specially sent Mr. Powell, the chief writer of the China Weekly Review, as a representative to the Chinese media and government to request a corresponding commemorative item, hoping to be given old stone objects. The Chinese government agreed to the request because the university people have given much support to the Chinese revolution and has trained many talents for the Chinese press. The government immediately sent people to Beijing and Shanghai to purchase and search for a satisfactory object, but it was difficult to find one for a long time. At the time, a pair of stone lions at Bao'en Temple in Beijing were being repaired. The Beijing Municipal Government stated that since the government needed to find stone objects to donate to the university, it could donate them. The National Government reported this to the National Government, which ordered Mr. Kong to transport the stone lions to the university on behalf of the government to promote China's inherent art. Dong Yu Accused by His Wife

▲Requesting Confirmation of Identity and Payment of Alimony

▲The Judge Attempted Reconciliation but Failed

Lawyer Dong Yu was recently sued in the District Court by his wife, Jiang, for abandonment, requesting confirmation of identity and payment of 10,000 yuan in alimony. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong Shenglie, accompanied by Clerk Huang Jiyuan, took the bench in the Second Tribunal to hear the case. Both parties were present in court as summoned. First, the plaintiff, Jiang, testified that she was 33 years old, from Anhui, and resided at 705 Jinwenfang, Seymour Road. (Question) What is the object of the request? (Answer) Confirmation of identity and request for 10,000 yuan in alimony. (Question) How to confirm? (Answer) After the death of [his first wife] Lu, the defendant said that Lu was his first wife. If so, then what am I to him? Before, in the tenth year of the Republic [1921], after the engagement but before the marriage, I knew that Lu had written a letter questioning [our relationship]. The letter was mediated by the defendant's cousin, Dong Banggan, who produced a letter proving my identity. The defendant also wrote a letter recognizing me as his legal wife, so he married me. On September 23rd of last year, my mother's family had a happy event, so I returned to Ning [Ningbo]. When I returned that night, I was suddenly rejected by the defendant. Shortly after, I returned to Ning again. When I returned to my husband's house, the defendant did not allow me to return home, so I lived in the house of the defendant's uncle, Dong Kang. (Question) At that time, was Lu already dead? (Answer) Yes, she was dead. (Question) Do you want to go back now? (Answer) He mistreats me, gives me a small room to live in, and does not allow servants to give me food. (Question) Do you want 10,000 yuan for living expenses? (Answer) Yes, calculated for 20 years. (Question) Do you know how much property he has? (Answer) He has property, such as deposits in the bank, because he said that I caused Lu's death and refused to live with me. Next, the defendant, Dong Yu, testified that he was 38 years old, from Wujin, and resided at Xiafei Square, Avenue Joffre. In February of the tenth year of the Republic [1921], he married Lu, and in October of the same year, he married Jiang. As for the question of Jiang's identity, now that Lu is dead, Jiang has been promoted to the position of legal wife. The plaintiff's purpose is nothing more than money. (Question) Does he agree to cohabitation? (Answer) A few days ago, her maternal grandfather had come to talk about it, [and we] are still cohabitating, but he walked out eighteen years ago. (Question) Was it to marry off his younger brother? (Answer) No, he lived with another person near the Baiyun Temple outside the West Gate. At that time, someone tried to persuade him to come back, but he said that he would rather die than go back. Afterwards, he wrote a letter asking for 6,000 yuan for support. I did not agree to it, but the reason he went out was that he was unwilling to work at home. After Lu died, I very much hoped that he would take charge of the inner quarters and manage the household, but he went out every day, so quarrels inevitably occurred. The official said that people who both have identities should not be involved in litigation. It is better to reconcile and cohabitate in court. At this point in the questioning, Jiang said, "The defendant said that after Lu died, he promoted me to the position of legal wife, then I am clearly a concubine. He also said that I went out with someone, who exactly should be pointed out." The official said, "Husbands and wives have a duty to cohabitate. I advise you to still share a room." She answered, "If we cohabitate, my life will be in danger." The official said, "What danger is there?" Thereupon, the questioner repeatedly tried to enlighten the plaintiff, who steadfastly refused to comply. Reconciliation failed, so the debate began. The lawyer hired by the plaintiff began to state the case. The questioner considered it to be concluded and set the verdict for the afternoon of the fourth of this month.

Fire in Houjiabang Kills a Woman

Burning Down a Three-Story Building

Staircase Burned Through, Woman Dies Tragically

Sun opened the Meili Sock Factory downstairs and sublet the second floor to Gu Haifan (36 years old) from Ningbo to open the Delong Ribbon Factory. Suddenly, at 3 a.m. on May 1, a fire broke out on the second floor and spread upwards and downwards. It was late at night when [people] noticed, and there was no way to put it out. The fire burst through the roof, and the flames were like a dragon. The North District Fire Brigade was the first to arrive by car, but the fire had already spread. Fire trucks from various districts arrived one after another and tried their best to extinguish the fire, which was finally extinguished at 4 a.m. A three-story building was burned down. When the fire was raging, the staircase connecting to the third floor was burned through. Zhou Yinshi (24 years old, from Shandong), who lived on the third floor, was unable to escape and burned to death. Yesterday, the body was retrieved and examined for cremation. The cause of the fire has not yet been determined. However, the Delong Ribbon Factory had fire insurance of 8,000 taels, and the Meili Sock Factory had 500 taels.

▲Yan Peiji, First Place for Residential Housing

After the Public Works Bureau's solicitation of standard designs for rental houses in the commercial and residential areas of the city center closed on April 15, the bureau sent letters to the Chinese Engineering Society, the Chinese Institute of Architects, and the Shanghai Architectural Association, inviting each organization to nominate a representative, and also sent separate letters to invite two people with a reputation in the architectural field in the city to form a judging committee. On the afternoon of the 27th of last month, the committee conducted a detailed examination and open selection at the Public Recreation Hall of the Municipal Government on Weihaiwei Road in accordance with the regulations of the solicitation method. Although the results of this solicitation were not satisfactory, the bureau, in order to encourage the interest of the applicants, still awarded prizes as usual. The winners of the commercial housing designs were: First Place: Zhuang Renqing; Second Place: Yan Peiji; Third Place: Tang Zhaoxiong, Shi Jusun. The winners of the residential housing designs were: First Place: Yan Peiji; Second Place: Tang Zhaoxiong, Shi Jusun; Third Place: Zhuang Renqing. The Public Works Bureau has officially announced that all winners can collect their respective prize money from the bureau.

Statistics on Traffic Accidents Last Month

The Ta Mei Wan Bao [Great American Evening News] reported that the number of traffic accidents in the Public Concession in April was lighter than in the previous month. According to the statistics of the Police Traffic Department, a total of four people died in the whole month, while there were seventeen in March, and the total for the first four months of this year reached thirty-seven. There were a total of 981 traffic accidents in the month, with 352 injuries, of which 747 involved cars, 127 involved trams, 94 involved public buses, and 127 involved bicycles. It was also found that the ages of the injured this month were: 17 under 7 years old, 46 between 7 and 15 years old, 268 between 15 and 60 years old, and 10 over 60 years old.

Construction of the First Municipal Cemetery Began Yesterday

▲The Cemetery is Located West of the Jiangwan Gaojing Temple Railway Station

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works and Sanitation had previously jointly submitted a proposal to the Municipal Government to establish a municipal cemetery. The cemetery site has four locations: Jiangwan, Pusong, Jing, and Pudong. Construction of the First Municipal Cemetery began yesterday. The cemetery is located west of the Jiangwan Gaojing Temple Railway Station, with an area of 200 mu. The construction cost is estimated to be about 100,000 yuan, which has been ordered by the Municipal Government to be allocated by the Municipal Finance Bureau.

▲Not Held Today

The Shanghai Volunteer Corps's annual grand review was originally scheduled for the 26th of last month. However, due to the unfavorable weather of continuous rainy days, it was proposed to postpone it to this Sunday. The country's authorities believe that the grand review should be held every year in April.

Since it was delayed due to rain and the deadline has passed, there is no need to postpone it again, so it was decided to cancel it and it will not be held today.

Housing Rent Dispute in Lizhongli

▲Reasons for the Landlord's Rent Increase

▲The Presiding Judge Still Advised Reconciliation

The case of rent increase in Lizhongli houses on Feihong Road, Hongzhen, this city, has been mediated twice by the Rent Dispute Arbitration Committee organized by the Shanghai Municipal Government, which considered the landlord's rent increase of 30% to be very reasonable and ordered the tenants to cancel the illegal Tenants' Self-Government Association. The tenants, fearing rejection, suddenly withdrew the mediation. Recently, the tenant representatives of the neighborhood suddenly sued the landlord Chen Changkun in the Shanghai District Court, requesting confirmation of the validity of the contract. Presiding Judge Guo Shouyi of the Civil Tribunal summoned [both parties] once on the 28th of this month and ordered them to go out for reconciliation. The afternoon before yesterday was the date for the continued hearing. After Judge Guo took the bench, he ordered both parties to present evidence. The landlord Chen Changkun presented a list of tenants in arrears of rent, the amount, and a cost budget table, as well as a list of tenants who had already increased the rent by 30%. The plaintiff's lawyer Chen Honglai stated that the former landlord, Jukang Qianzhuang, allowed a temporary postponement of the rent increase, and the current landlord should not increase the rent because the previous contract continued to be valid. Then, the defendant's lawyer Zhou Xiaoan argued that the letter from Jukangzhuang only contained the phrase "it seems possible to postpone temporarily," and anyone with a little knowledge of the text knows that it is an empty and uncertain term. Since it was not determined, this contract cannot be valid, and the rent in Lizhongli was originally 20 yuan per building for shikumen and 16 yuan per building for Guangshi. After Shanghai was affiliated with the National Government, shikumen was reduced to 15 yuan and Guangshi was reduced to 12 yuan. Last year, the former landlord increased shikumen by one yuan per building, only 16 yuan, and Guangshi by 5 jiao, only 12 and a half yuan. This rent is lower than the nearby Yuezhoufang and Dongjun'anli. Now that gold is expensive and silver is cheap, and everything is expensive, and land prices are soaring, the defendant paid nearly 180,000 taels when purchasing this neighborhood's land last year. With the current low rent, it is not enough to cover the interest. Therefore, in addition to requesting the rejection of the plaintiff's lawsuit, [we] are also filing a counterclaim and requesting Lizhongli to increase the rent by 30%. After the rent increase, each shikumen building will only be 20 yuan and 4 jiao, which is still low compared to the rent in this city. [We] also request a judgment ordering the tenants to pay the arrears of rent and ordering [them] to vacate the house. Afterwards, Judge Guo advised both parties to reconcile: 1. From July 1, the rent will be increased by 2 yuan per building. 2. Sign a shorter contract. 3. Arrears of rent must be paid. Both parties complied with the instructions and went out to try to reconcile, and then adjourned.

Xue's Son-in-Law Withdraws the Property Dispute Lawsuit

Hua Lihou, the son-in-law of the deceased paint merchant Xue Yinrun, brought his two sons, Yiweng and Yigu, and daughter Manyun, hiring three lawyers, Zhang Jiahui, Ye Shaoying, and Yang Linzhi, to represent him in suing his mother-in-law Xue Sun, his brothers-in-law Xue Jing sheng, Yansheng, Jiasheng, Gensheng, etc., in the French Concession Civil Court for the occupation of the estate and failure to divide it. The previous reports have already noted that the defendants were ordered to personally surrender to the court for questioning. Yesterday, the defendants were again summoned and each complied with the order to appear in court. The plaintiff's lawyer suddenly submitted a petition requesting the withdrawal of the case. The defendants' representatives, lawyers Lin Yingqing and Wang Yintai, both stated that the plaintiff's side suddenly filed a lawsuit and suddenly requested a withdrawal. [We] should request the court to reject it and approve the counterclaim for the plaintiff's debt. Judge Gong ruled that since the case had not yet begun to be argued, the plaintiff's request for withdrawal was considered appropriate. [He] ruled that the plaintiff's request for withdrawal should be approved and that the defendant's request for a counterclaim should be filed separately.

Two Counterfeit Money Organizations Cracked Down in the French Concession

Zhang Xingwu from Shandong recently privately set up an organization for selling counterfeit money in Room 53, Oriental Apartments, Avenue Baille, French Concession. The French Concession Police Detective Bao found out about it and arrested Zhang at the place the day before yesterday, seizing 4,000 yuan of five-yuan and ten-yuan banknotes and taking [him] into custody. Then, [they] found out that there was also a selling organization at 73 Run'an Lane, Ximen Road, and went to arrest Han Ronghua, seizing 20 counterfeit banknotes and more than 70 yuan in cash from [his] person. Afterwards, [they] successively apprehended suspects Liu Jizhang, Chen Qingchang, Liu Jianfeng, etc. and took them into custody. Yesterday, they were sent to the French Concession Court for questioning. First, the police chief reported the previous situation and presented the counterfeit banknotes for inspection. Zhang Xingwu confessed that the banknotes were entrusted to the people by someone surnamed Zhang who lived in the Nanjing Hotel to sell on his behalf, but the whereabouts of Zhang are unknown. Han Ronghua confessed that the people and Zhang Xingwu were friends and that Zhang Xingwu entrusted me to sell these counterfeit banknotes on his behalf. The rest of the confession was vague. When questioned, Liu Jizhang and others confessed that the people did not know about the private sale of banknotes. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Zhang Xingwu to three years in the Western Jail and Han Ronghua to two years. Liu Jizhang and the other three were released without charge. The counterfeit banknotes in the seized case were destroyed.

Ye Chen Lawsuit Postponed for Further Hearing

The case of Ye Zhongfang and dancer Chen Xiuzhen mutually suing each other in the French Concession Court was again summoned yesterday. Ye Zhongfang, Ye Peng, Ye Lu, etc. still did not appear in court. The acting lawyer Dong Yu stated that the plaintiff Ye Peng was visiting Ningbo with her daughter-in-law Lu because her aunt was ill, causing Zhongfang to experience mental stimulation and is now being treated in the hospital, so none of them could attend this time and requested a postponement for further examination. Chen Xiuzhen's representative, lawyer Yao Zhaodi, stated that the statements of the opposing counsel were probably untrue and that someone had recently seen Ye Zhongfang still going in and out of dance halls. The truth is that he intentionally evaded attendance. Judge Zhu ruled that Ye Zhongfang, Ye Peng, and Ye Lu should not have been summoned twice without attendance. Each should be fined 2 yuan and the hearing postponed for seven days for another summons.

Due to Communist Suspicions, Cheng Yongxi Was Finally Transferred

Cheng Yongxi from Anhui practiced medicine and hung his pot at 535 Baek Road. Last winter, the Municipal Public Security Bureau learned that he had previously served in Zhang Fakui's Communist army as a military doctor. In the winter of the sixteenth year of the Republic [1927], Zhang's army burned and killed the Cantonese city, and Cheng also worked in Guangzhou, so he was suspected of being a Communist. [The Bureau] jointly apprehended and sent [him] to the Special District Local Court, which ordered that he be handed over to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Because the police were dissatisfied, they filed an appeal and the extradition was not actually carried out. Recently, the Higher Branch Court revoked the preliminary hearing decision and returned it to the Special District Court for re-examination. On the 28th of last month, Judge Wu Tingqi re-examined the result and still ruled that [Cheng] should be taken by the Public Security Bureau and sent to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. The police lawyer again requested that the execution be suspended during the appeal period, so although Cheng had been decided to be extradited twice, he was not finally extradited. Yesterday morning, the police lawyer Zhang Tianyin specially declared to the original judge that the Public Works Bureau had decided to abandon the appeal in this case and that the inland officials could take [him] away. Judge Wu learned that Director Chen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau had sent Section Chief Ding Jun of the Third Section to the court to receive [him]. [He] then handed over Cheng [Yongxi] to Section Chief Ding in court and turned [him] over to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. This case has been delayed for more than half a year and can be considered over.

Social Bureau Orders the Hengda Yarn Factory to Resume Work Tomorrow

▲Awaiting the Authorities to Investigate and Verify

After the workers of the Hengda Yarn Factory in Yangsi Bridge, Pudong, opposed the factory's transfer of workers and went on strike, the factory announced a temporary shutdown. The Municipal Social Bureau ordered the factory to resume work tomorrow and await verification. The various circumstances are recorded as follows:

Mediation Meeting

The Municipal Social Bureau convened a labor-capital question-and-answer session at 3 p.m. the day before yesterday (the 1st) to conduct mediation. The representatives present were Zhang Sheng from the Municipal Citizen Training Association, Chen Zixing and Zhu Yufang from the capital side, and Zhang Qingyun and Qin A'fa from the labor side. The meeting was chaired by Zhu Guilin from the Social Bureau. The labor's demands were: 1. Resume work as soon as possible. 2. Punish the staff who abuse workers. 3. Release the innocent arrested workers. 4. Wages should be paid as usual during the shutdown period. The capital's demand was to dismiss the troublemaking workers. The chairman advised to resume work first and the rest to await investigation and verification. The capital representatives insisted on the order of General Manager Rong Zongjing to wait for the workers to fill in the guarantee before resuming work, so the problem was not solved.

Order to Resume Work

The Municipal Social Bureau ordered the Hengda Yarn Factory yesterday, saying that it had received the report. It was found that the factory should give priority to supplementing workers and that the factory should be responsible for the disturbance caused by the unwarranted placement of new workers. In addition to approving the workers to resume work and investigating and verifying the workers' insurance policy and other labor-capital disputes separately, you must comply with the order to resume work as usual on the 4th of this month without delay. This batch also orders the trade union to resume work uniformly.

Changes After Arbitration of the Jinxin Factory Labor Dispute

▲The Labor Side Petitions the Municipal Government to Submit It to the Court for Execution

The Jinxin Silk Weaving Factory on Avenue Saussier in the French Concession has been on strike for more than a month. After six mediations by the Social Bureau failed, it was submitted to arbitration for resolution and the resumption of work was scheduled for April 27. Unexpectedly, there were twists and turns on that day, extending to the resumption of work on May 1. Unexpectedly, another change occurred on the due date. The First Special District Silk Weaving Industry Trade Union Preparatory Committee's document to the Municipal Government is recorded as follows: The strike at Jinxin has been submitted to the court for execution after the arbitration decision by your government. The factory side has no sincerity at all and has been using excuses to delay and refuse to resume work. The loss fee was changed to the voluntary dissolution fee when a strike occurs in the future without authorization, and the workers are forced to sign, hoping to destroy the labor movement invisibly. However, the workers, most of whom are illiterate, almost fell into their trap. However, after going back and forth several times, not only was the fee not issued, but it was even claimed that the arbitration was overturned. Then, lawyer Lu Qi was entrusted to announce the calling of the board. Therefore, this is a special presentation. Please approve the submission to the court for prompt execution and warn the lawyer to benefit the labor movement (omitted below).

Central Bank Inspection Report

▲88th Inspection

The 88th inspection report on the issuance reserve of the Central Bank states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Ordinance, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the bank's issuance of convertible banknotes. The 88th inspection was held at the bank's issuance bureau on April 30, 1931. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: Total amount of convertible banknotes issued: Silver dollars 31,515,082, including silver dollar notes of 30,073,312 yuan and subsidiary currency notes of 1,441,770 yuan. Total reserve fund: Silver dollars 31,515,082, including cash reserve of silver dollars 24,442,483.1 yuan. The cash reserve includes 17,260,962.35 yuan stored in the bank's issuance vault, 2,127,638 yuan stored in branches in various ports, 5,053,880.75 yuan stored with the same, and security reserve equivalent to 7,072,598.9 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the security reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60%, and the security is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. April 30, 1931. Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank: Li Fusun, Supervisors: Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Ji.

Ministry of Industry to Conduct Survey on Business Conditions

▲Instruction to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "The Ministry of Industry has issued Instruction No. 829, stating that the Ministry is conducting a survey on the general conditions of commercial firms in various counties and cities domestically. Survey forms for the general conditions of commercial firms have been prepared and should be issued to the relevant departments in each province and city for distribution to the county governments or chambers of commerce. They should be filled out in detail with reference to the attached Provisional Classification Standards for Commercial Firms by Industry and submitted to the bureaus by the end of August this year, to be presented to the Ministry for statistical compilation. In addition to separate orders, a thousand copies of the commercial firm table and five hundred copies of the classification standards are hereby issued, ordering the bureau to comply and instruct the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to earnestly handle the matter. The completed forms should be submitted to the bureau by July 15th of this year for forwarding, without delay. This order is hereby issued." The attached survey form specifies the following items: (A) Organization: (1) Sole proprietorship, (2) Partnership, (3) Unlimited liability company, (4) Limited partnership, (5) Limited liability company, (6) Joint-stock limited partnership, (7) Remarks. (B) Item: (1) Number of firms, (2) Total capital amount, (3) Number of employees, (4) Total business turnover last year. (C) Industry. (D) Instructions: (1) This form can be used to survey all shops, halls, firms, offices, or companies that engage in the sale of goods, financial circulation, regulation of social personnel supply and demand, and the handling of fire, water, personal, and life insurance. (2) The type of business should be filled in for each industry, and the names of each business can be adopted according to the Provisional Classification Standards for Commercial Firms by Industry. (3) Capital must be calculated in Chinese silver dollars; those calculated in non-Chinese silver dollars should be converted into Chinese silver dollars. (4) If there are several foreign firms within the number of firms in a certain industry, in addition to filling in the number of firms in the "Number of Firms in a Certain Industry" column, the number of foreign firms must also be noted in the "Remarks" column. For example, if there are ten partnerships in the art and craft sales industry in Shanghai, and two of them are operated by British and three by Germans, when filling out the form, not only should "10" be filled in the "Partnership" column of the art and craft sales industry, but also "Partnership: British 2, German 3" should be filled in the "Remarks" column. (5) If there is foreign capital within the capital of a certain industry's commercial firms, in addition to filling in the total capital amount of the commercial firms in that industry in the "Capital Amount of the Commercial Firm" column, the original amount of foreign capital and its converted amount in Chinese silver dollars must also be noted in the "Remarks" column. For example, if the US dollar of the Nanjing textile craft sales industry is converted into Chinese yuan and added to the total amount of 100,000 Chinese yuan, it should be filled in the "Capital Amount" column of the "Unlimited Liability Company" in that industry, and it must also be noted that the amount of US dollars is 10,000 and its converted Chinese yuan amount, with the note "Converted according to the market price at what time" in the "Remarks" column. (6) If there are several foreign employees within the number of employees of a certain industry's commercial firms, in addition to filling in the total number of employees in the "Number of Employees in a Certain Industry" column, the number of foreign employees must also be noted in the "Remarks" column. For example, if there are ten partnerships in the art and craft sales industry in Shanghai, and the total number of employees is one hundred, including five British employees and three German employees, when filling out the form, not only should "100" be filled in the "Number of Employees" column of the partnership commercial firm in the art and craft sales industry, but also "Partnership: British 5, German 3" should be filled in the "Remarks" column. (7) The business turnover amount must be calculated in Chinese silver dollars; those calculated in non-Chinese silver dollars should be converted into Chinese silver dollars. (8) If a part of the total business turnover of a certain industry's commercial firms is the business turnover of foreign commercial firms, in addition to filling in the total business turnover amount in the "Certain Industry's Commercial Firm" column, the total business turnover amount of foreign commercial firms must also be noted in the "Remarks" column. For example, if there are ten partnerships in the art and craft sales industry in Shanghai, and the business turnover is 150,000 yuan, of which the business turnover of two British-operated firms is 30,000 yuan, and the business turnover of three German-operated firms is 45,000 yuan, when filling out the form, not only should 150,000 yuan be filled in the "Partnership" column of the art and craft sales industry, but also "Partnership: British 30,000 yuan, German 45,000 yuan" should be filled in the "Remarks" column.

Gao Linsheng Robbed and Extorted, Imprisoned for Eight Years

▲The Murder Portion is Transferred to the Inland Court for Trial

Gao Linsheng, also known as Zhou Mulin, from Pudong, committed crimes in Shanghai. On March 16th of this year, he and his accomplices held weapons and robbed Wu Zicheng's house at No. 423, Ma Le Li, Chongqing Road, of property worth more than 790 yuan. Later, he sent a letter to Shen Liusheng, the owner of the Shen Tai Construction Factory on Ningbo Road, extorting 30,000 yuan. At that time, Shen urgently needed to go to Tianjin because he had contracted a project there, so he did not report the case to the police. Gao was arrested by the Yangshupu Police Station before he could continue to extort money. It was also found that Gao, in addition to robbery and extortion, was also involved in the assassination of water police officer Pang Gongyi. Yesterday afternoon, the police escorted the bandit to the Special District Local Court, where Magistrate Feng Shide interrogated him. According to the police lawyer Li Zhishan, the robbery case had been investigated with the victim present, and although the victim in the extortion case had gone to Tianjin, a representative was present to explain the process. It was heard that the accomplice Gu A'er had been captured in the Nanhui County assassination case and could be brought by the Public Security Bureau because the case occurred inland. Therefore, Tang Renqi, an employee of Shen Liusheng, testified that Shen received a threatening letter by post last month asking him to negotiate at the Oriental Hotel. Shen suspected that it was jealousy from his peers, but he did not receive a second letter and did not report the case to the police. The defendant fully admitted to the robbery and blamed his friend for dictating the threatening letter. He hesitated and stammered in his confession of the assassination. After investigation and trial, Magistrate Feng immediately sentenced Gao Linsheng to seven years in prison for carrying a weapon and committing armed robbery, and two years for attempted extortion, to be served concurrently for a total of eight years. The murder portion will be handed over to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau for submission to the inland court for trial.

Writing Fees of Cheng Kai Zhou

Mr. Cheng Zhoukai of Xin'an is famous for his writing throughout the eight districts of Anhui, and his calligraphy is especially skilled. He came to Shanghai this spring. Mr. Huang Binhong, Xu Danfu, Wang Zhongqi, Xu Bolong, and other fellow villagers have helped him set writing fees: One yuan per foot for couplets, two yuan per foot for scrolls and horizontal banners, the same as couplets for each foot of screens, plus half for single strips, four yuan per piece for albums, three yuan per character within one foot for plaques, six yuan for those larger than one foot, sixteen yuan per article for inscriptions, biographies, longevity prefaces, and genealogy prefaces, negotiable fees for elegies and eulogies, eight yuan per article for epilogues and praises, five yuan per piece for ancient and modern poems (limited rhymes, doubled for limited words and embedded characters), a 10% fee for ink. Payment is required before delivery, and the collection date is agreed upon. The temporary collection point is No. 20 Zhenpingli, Songshan Road, French Concession, Huining School, and Mr. Wang Jianwei of the Xinwen Newspaper.

Xinhua Launches Life Savings Deposit

After the reorganization and opening of the Xinhua Trust and Savings Bank, it has been actively engaged in various trust and savings businesses. Recently, it launched a five-year life savings deposit, which started accepting deposits yesterday. The method is very novel. Five years is set as one term. People aged 16 to 60 with legitimate occupations can recognize deposits of three yuan per month. After five years, they can recover a principal and interest of 200 yuan. If an accident occurs in the middle, they can also receive a savings compensation of 200 yuan. The idea of combining insurance with savings is intended to benefit store employees, factory workers, and the general self-employed. In order to protect the safety of life savings depositors, the bank has specially allocated 100,000 yuan as a reserve fund to organize an inspection committee with transparent and independent accounting.

Yongda Electrical Materials Store Grand Opening Yesterday

Since its opening, Yongda Electrical Materials Store on Fourth Road has been doing well. Manager Huang Jiafu has specially established a new headquarters at No. 74 Daxin Street. Yesterday was the official opening day, and both the new and old stores offered discounts and gifts. After 9:00 a.m., there were more than a thousand Chinese and foreign guests, such as Mr. Wang Xiaoyi and the heads of Philips and Siemens, who came to congratulate them. Shao Ruxin and Wang Yuqing cordially greeted them, serving tea and snacks and accompanying them to view the store's various novel products. On that day, the store was crowded with retail and wholesale customers, receiving a total of tens of thousands of dollars in business from packaging projects.

German Military Officer Ink Sold at Original Price

Since the wave of gold being expensive and silver being cheap has shaken the world, countries with silver standards have rarely escaped its severe impact. Not only has the price of various commodities been directly affected and soared, but also the spiritual and cultural development has been indirectly affected and become stagnant. The German Military Officer Brand Ink Store on Fifth Road West, Shanghai, has a long-standing reputation for selling German Military Officer Brand Ink in Shanghai and abroad. This is because this kind of military officer brand ink has bright colors and pure materials, which are completely different from the sticky, oily, and dull inferior goods. In recent months, the prices of all European, American, and Japanese inks have risen sharply. Only this store has not raised the price of military officer ink in order to compensate for the obstacles to printing and cultural development. The most commonly used ordinary red, blue, yellow, and white inks are now reduced in price again, with red and blue selling for only 8.5 jiao per pound and yellow and white for only 4.5 jiao per pound.

Achievements of Sun Shihao's Solo Exhibition

Sun Shihao's solo exhibition at the Chinese Science Society on Albert Road has been a great success since its opening. Western paintings such as "Night Tour of Chibi," "Beauty," "Human Body," and "Flowers," as well as Chinese paintings such as "Taishi," "Yanliu," "Horses," and "Birds," have all been purchased by connoisseurs. There is no shortage of people who have booked paintings.

Record of the Shareholders' Meeting of China Express Company

The China Express Company held its annual shareholders' meeting on April 25th at its Shanghai headquarters. Shareholders Wu Yunqi, Qian Xinzhi, Shen Chuchen, and others were present, representing 9,360 shares. General Manager Yu Yanfang reported on the company's business operations, stating that although freight transportation was sluggish in 1919 due to the impact of the war, the company adhered to a prudent policy and reduced expenditures, so it still made a slight profit. Subsequently, Wang Yiting, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Rutang, Yu Jitong, Wu Yunqi, Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Woyun, Yu Yanfang, Du Meishu, and others were elected as directors, and Ding Ziying and Zhu Bangsheng were elected as supervisors. It is reported that the company will issue dividends from today.

The Guangdong Grand Theater has spared no expense to hire the famous Cantonese opera troupe New Spring and Autumn Troupe to perform in Shanghai. Record of the Meeting of the Cattle and Sheep Industry

The Shanghai Cattle and Sheep Industry Association held a special meeting yesterday because the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance ordered the association to pay the repeated cattle and sheep inspection fees for 1919. Hundreds of members attended the meeting, which was chaired by Chen Guanghai. The meeting began at 2:00 p.m. to discuss the matter. As a result, based on the principle of "one item, one tax," the members opposed the arbitrary collection of inspection fees and were willing to share the expenses of sanitary inspection.

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor:

I read in your newspaper on the 25th of this month that the Jiangsu Higher Court sent personnel to tour and try cases of Red Bandits and bandits in various counties. After investigation, this court has legally designated the local court to send magistrates to participate in the temporary tribunals organized by the county governments to try these cases after the implementation of the Emergency Crime Punishment Law for Endangering the Republic of China. There is no such thing as sending personnel to tour and try cases of Red Bandits and bandits in various counties. The report in your newspaper is a rumor. I hereby inform you and hope you will check and publish this letter in the letter column to correct it.

Respectfully,

Jiangsu Higher Court

April 28

Dear Mr. Chief Editor of Shenbao:

I recently read in the news column of your newspaper on April 28th that a retired soldier from Hunan, Hu Bin, ran out of money and was rescued after throwing himself into the Huangpu River. He has been sent to the local court for relief. I feel deeply saddened.

I have fought on the battlefield for many years and have experienced many hardships. I cannot help but shed tears of sympathy for the soldiers at the end of their road. Although I have a humble position and limited ability, I am still willing to sacrifice my salary to help the destitute. I believe that the compassionate chief editor also has a heart of compassion. Please forward this letter to the court or charitable organization to provide travel expenses so that he can quickly come to the Investigation Team of the Jinpu Railway Garrison Headquarters on Sanma Road, Xuzhou. I will arrange for him to fill a military position so that he can continue to serve the army and avoid the recurrence of world-weariness. This act of kindness will be bestowed by the chief editor.

Respectfully yours,

Tong Chuanduo

In Support of Good Wives and Wise Mothers

— Tao Zaidong

Since the rise of non-filial piety arguments and the slogan to overthrow "good wives and wise mothers," informed individuals are worried. I believe that good wives and wise mothers are treasures of the nation. Not only should they not be overthrown, but there is a real need to support them. Moved by the conduct of my own two mothers throughout my life, I describe it to inform my fellow countrymen.

One is Mother Zhang, the wife of Zhang Ziyun of Kunming in the same year. Ziyun was appointed magistrate through the imperial examinations, serving in Yongfeng, Jiangxi, and later transferred to Leping and Qingjiang. He was known for his integrity as an official. He passed away at the end of the Guangxu era, leaving behind a desolate family with many children. Mother Zhang supported the family and completed her husband's official duties. Later, when Jiangxi was restored and banditry arose, she could not return to her hometown tens of thousands of miles away. She led her children to the sea, enduring extreme hardship for thirty years. Her moral integrity was unwavering, and her actions were commonplace. I feel that while her ordinary conduct may not be suitable for grand praise, her hardship and integrity should not be forgotten. Recently, her two sons have completed their studies and are serving society. Mother Zhang wisely helped them choose good sons-in-law. One of them is the famous doctor Cai Jiping. Now, her eldest grandson, Naiyang, has graduated from Guanghua University and works in a bank. The family is happy and prosperous. My friend, if he knew in the afterlife, would not have lamented the impossibility of being an honest official. By this time, Mother Zhang had passed her sixtieth year and suffered from wind-dampness due to accumulated fatigue for five or six years. In the chaos of Hunan and Jiangxi, many families of gentry and officials were ruined, but the Zhang family prospered. Whose strength was this due to? The nation is an accumulation of families. If every family has a good wife and wise mother, then the nation will have nurtured men and educated women. Isn't this the most hard-working, most compassionate, formless yet spiritual public nursery?

The other is Mother Qian, the mother of my friend Qian Wenxuan of Guangde. In his early years, Qian Wenxuan was recommended by the Ministry of Education to study in England as a supervisor for overseas students. Later, he served as a consul in the United States, traveled around the globe, and attended international cultural and racial conferences, becoming well-known in diplomatic circles. After returning to China, he served as an official for a long time with a reputation for integrity and competence. In the eighth year of the Republic, he strenuously persuaded Tang Jiyao to abandon the Yunnan Doctrine and implement armed participation in the war. He traveled between Feng and Duan, seeking the unification of China, which nearly succeeded but ultimately failed. The telegrams are still preserved, excellent historical materials. He is considered a talented individual, and it is not just flattery. Qian Wenxuan's life story is particularly unique. His ancestors moved from Liyang to Guangde, where the clan numbered five hundred people, gradually dwindling. By the time Wenxuan was born, his father had died at the age of four, and the entire clan depended on him alone. This was indeed precarious. His mother, Dai Lizhi, upheld her integrity, raised her orphaned son, and endured all kinds of hardships to achieve what he is today. Now Wenxuan has four sons and one grandson. The middle son, Ruoyang and Ruojin, is especially lovable and capable of writing. Is the continuation of the Qian clan not due to Dai's efforts? It is regrettable that Mother Qian passed away before Wenxuan became famous. Official honors and posthumous recognition are all things that can only be done after death. For the son, there is the profound grief of sacrificing an ox to enjoy at her tomb. But for the mother, she would be content to have fulfilled her filial duty. Examining the laws of various countries regarding relatives, only Chinese parents bear absolute obligations without rights, yet stories of wise mothers are constantly written. Is this due to the effectiveness of laws or the merit of moral education? How can one deny and overthrow them?

Puree Talk

— Chen Boying

Among the vegetables used to enrich meals in a timely manner, water shield (蓴菜) is now highly regarded. Water shield can be used to make soup, generally with tender bamboo shoots, shredded ham, and shredded fragrant mushrooms. It can also be cooked in chicken soup, which makes it especially delicious. Although water shield borrows the flavors of other ingredients, its smooth and slippery texture is unmatched by other dishes, so it has a unique flavor. Water shield grows in the lakes of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces; it is not produced elsewhere. Its leaves are green and oval-shaped, with long stalks and a sticky liquid on the back of the leaves. This is what makes it smooth and slippery when eaten. It is tenderest in the spring, blossoms in the summer (when it is not suitable for eating), and becomes tough in the autumn. During the Jin dynasty, Zhang Jiaying was an aide to the Prince of Qi. One day, seeing the autumn wind rise, he thought of the wild rice stems and water shield soup and bass he had back in his hometown of Wu, and he immediately ordered his carriage to return. Such a small matter of diet was enough to overcome his official aspirations. Also, Lu Ji visited Wang Ji, who pointed to sheep cheese and asked Lu, "What in Wu can match this?" Lu replied, "A thousand-mile water shield soup has not yet been served." At that time, it was considered a famous reply and an anecdote. The character "莼" is sometimes written as "蒓".

The Blind Person with Unusual Sense of Smell

— Xu Xiaoting

Ears can hear sounds, eyes can distinguish colors, and the nose manages breathing and differentiates fragrances and odors. I have never heard of using the nose to replace the eyes. Looking at the blind in the past, those who use their ears to replace their eyes still cannot avoid the criticism of groping and probing. The nose is merely a breathing tube. Now, it can actually recognize objects and distinguish colors with infallible accuracy. This is truly an extraordinary and strange matter.

Wang Runian, a blind person in the city, was born blind. He has never personally seen the myriad things in society, but his sense of smell is extremely acute. He can identify any object he touches with his nose. The most unusual thing is that if there are several people present, he can identify each of them by smelling them, even if they remain silent. He has been tested repeatedly and the results are always accurate. Wang's sense of smell is truly extraordinary and beyond the reach of ordinary people. When people ask him what method he uses to distinguish between them, Wang says, "The skin and sweat glands of people have different smells. In the cold weather of winter, everyone produces little sweat, and I can only tell them apart by touching their skin. But in the summer, as soon as someone is ten steps away, I can tell who it is." My (the reporter's) friend Qian Xueming, who lives in Yancheng, once tried to make it difficult for him, so he took more than a dozen sheets of red and white paper, mixed them up on a table, and asked if he could distinguish the colors of the paper. Wang agreed readily, without any difficulty. He touched and smelled the paper and, within a few minutes, had separated the red paper from the white. At this time, Qian was extremely surprised and asked how he distinguished them. Wang said, "Colored paper has a different smell than colorless paper. It is not at all unusual for me to identify objects and colors by smell." When Mr. Qian told me about this, I was very surprised and said to Qian, "Although this blind man is blind in his eyes, he is not blind in his heart. His sense of smell is truly extraordinary and beyond the reach of ordinary people. But it is very strange to rely on smell to identify things and even to distinguish the colors of objects. The mystery within this is truly difficult for us to understand at this time."

A Record of the Peonies in Ye Garden

— Yu Jianhua

Those who have visited the Ye Garden in Jiangwan praise its pavilions, gardens, flowers, and trees as the best in the southeast. I have already written an article to record it. Recently, I heard that the peonies are in full bloom. I imagined that there were only three or four plants in the Agarwood Pavilion of the Immortal Spring Hall, because plants in the South are rare and not as easy to see as in the North, so I went to see them. When I entered the garden, I saw the mountain peaks, the water's edge, the rocks, and the roots of the trees arranged almost everywhere, probably numbering several thousand. The Yao Yellow, Wei Purple, brocade robes, and sandalwood hearts shone like a row of clouds, beautiful as displayed brocades. Some were deep red, some were pink clouds, some swayed in the wind, some drooped with dew, some curled up like phoenix tails, some were like orangutan lips, some were like a beauty's fresh makeup, and some were like Yang Guifei slightly drunk. Their red light, purple brilliance, rosy clusters, and cloud masses, with their unique postures and extraordinary appearances, truly deserve to overwhelm all the flowers and lead the way of the fragrant blossoms without shame. Therefore, I sighed in admiration. Peonies originally came from Luoyang, spread to Caozhou, and flourished in Yanjing. Now, times and situations have changed, and peonies will also move to better places. It is a pity that time was short and I did not have time to photograph the flowers. I returned and wrote this to tell people who are addicted to flowers to hurry up and take a look before the spring rain ruins them, the setting sun fades, and their dreams are scattered, and they are left facing the east wind with a broken heart.

A Record of Reading Paintings at the Guanhai Art Society

— Dan Shiyi

In early April, my friend Mr. Wu Lisheng came from the countryside to enjoy the fragrant flowers with me. Lisheng is also skilled in the arts and loves to explore calligraphy and painting. I had previously become acquainted with Mr. Zhao Anzhi of the Guanhai Society. Anzhi is skilled in the six principles of painting, learning from the Song and Yuan dynasty styles, with lofty ideas and magnificent colors. He has long enjoyed a great reputation, so we went together to visit him. The society's address is in Taoyuan Village. In the afternoon, we took a trip to the western suburbs. The green shade was like embroidery, and our hearts and minds were opened up. By the time we arrived at the gate, we saw the plaque written by Chu Minyi hanging there. We knocked on the door and Anzhi greeted us. We first admired the famous works hanging on the walls, many of which were ethereal works by people from the Song, Yuan, and Ming dynasties. We also examined the album leaves, with Zhao Zigu's paintings of peach blossoms being the most exquisite. Mr. Wu, who had long studied Anzhi's painting fame, requested to see his works, so he first showed us twelve album leaves imitating Song dynasty flower and bird paintings. The colors used were mostly made by the imperial palace and were not available to ordinary people. The workmanship was exquisite, lifelike and dazzling. We also saw four screen paintings imitating the works of Zhou Shaogu and Zhao Zigu, which had recently been brought back from overseas and were specially commissioned for the country's exposition, where they received excellent awards. Foreigners have always admired Chinese art, but they have always thought that Song and Yuan meticulous brushwork might not be known to outsiders. It is evident that the spread of national quintessence abroad depends on Anzhi. Gradually, we also reviewed Lin Baoshanzi's hand scrolls, etc. Chu Minyi, Wang Yiting, and other gentlemen all provided inscriptions. Mr. Wu then inquired about the source of his strength. Anzhi modestly said that he worked hard to learn and did not dare to take credit. We then inquired about his contact address. Anzhi said that he was not often in Shanghai. If there were any commissions, they could be forwarded through Mr. Wang Yunyi of the Banque de l'Indochine in the Bund, Shanghai. Mr. Wu thanked him for his hospitality and discussed issues such as the imitation of pigments. It was dusk when we left. I was very happy to have had the opportunity to see so many famous works, so I especially wrote this record.

Correction: In the title "Brief History of Zheng Zheneng, Inventor of Consecutive Rings," the character "發" (fā, invent) was mistakenly printed as "達" (dá, reach). This is hereby corrected.

Travelogue of India (42)

— Linghua

It was already late in the day when we returned to the rest room. Along the way, we bought various photos and there were many beggars, so we did not have time to give to everyone. We took a car back and the moon hung in the treetops, the lamplight reflecting off the water. The bright moon could be seen in the water. My jacket was quite cold. We returned to the rest area in Gaya Town. It was already eleven o'clock. I picked up some stones by the Mu Nu River. My companions and I drank its water, which was very sweet. The Buddha used to drink this water and became a Buddha. We also drank it. On this trip, I gained a lot of insights, so I wrote a poem to commemorate it. However, one thing is worth pondering: The Buddha traveled to the high peaks of the Himalayas and the boundless sea, but attained enlightenment in this small village. Is this accidental? Also, the Buddha sat facing east, gazing at the morning star, and attained perfect enlightenment. Is this the morning star in the East, or is it the star of his enlightened nature? I once fasted for seven days and suddenly one day, a fight broke out. I also saw a very bright starlight in my head, but this was not perfect enlightenment, which can be taken as a joke. The poem is as follows: Not dwelling by high mountains or the sea, a hill and a valley bring forth a heavenly man. The Saha world is full of Avatamsaka realms, realizing no birth is being an immortal. The traces of the shepherdess remain on the small slope, in those days, milk was offered to the Buddha. What need is there to speak of a ten-thousand-gold meal? Chickens and dogs all ascend to immortality and enter the Great Luo. The waters of the Bakusha River are clear and blue, small fish wag their tails and swim freely. When will sentient beings have the chance to be saved? Vainly in the Buddha's house, not yet free from birth. The ancient Bodhi tree is still swaying, how many times has it seen people become Buddhas? A pair of footprints can still be distinguished, here the Great Hero abandoned his charming lady. The Buddha faces west, facing east, the morning star shines on the true void above. The great and vast one can be a teacher, several courtyard flowers reflect the sun. I returned on a cold night after two hours, the slanting moon shining dimly through the forest. The Dharma assembly along the way is still flourishing, crowned with flower wreaths, transformed into affectionate beings. The Taoists here are half like opera singers, smearing their foreheads and wearing flower wreaths, and the singers listen quietly. In Buddha's time, it was also singing.

On the 24th, I got up early at 6 o'clock and took a car to Benares. We passed the river bridge to Benares. This river is the upper reaches of the Ganges River. The water is clear and pleasant. At the second station, Lawyer Mukherji and several others welcomed us to a Western woman's house. After resting and eating, the monks went to Sarnath. I stayed with Lawyer Mukherji at the home of Mr. Sen, an Indian. Mr. Sen is a wealthy merchant, 30 years old and single. He said that he wanted to go to the Himalayan mountains in the future. This is the Indian view of life. The room was decorated like a Japanese one, taking off one's shoes to enter. Short tables were used for writing. In winter, thick straw mats were laid. Many guests came. A secretary of a small king came to ask about the situation in China. Everyone was very happy because India very much hopes that China will be strong. A friend said, "I very much want to wear Chinese boots. If you wear British shoes or British goods, you will be torn apart." A certain lawyer wanted to marry a Chinese woman or said that Chinese was difficult to learn. I said it was not difficult. Being able to recognize three thousand characters allows you to read any book. The grammar is simple and not as clumsy as Western languages. The topics of speeches by scholars from various places were mostly about the revival of Eastern culture, recognizing the close relationship between Chinese and Indian cultures.

The Novel Promotion Society

Hawthorne's Detective Case: The Turn (2)

— Cheng Xiaoqing

He, who was the focus of the guests' attention, insisted on pestering me for a while, forcing me to dance, and then picking up a few difficult sentences from Shakespeare's plays and nagging me to explain them. For him, it was innocent and carefree, but in my position, to avoid misunderstandings among the general public, I had to be reserved. But there was no way to escape, so I felt a little embarrassed. Later, I was only a little freer when it came time to sit down. I originally wanted to sit for a while and then say goodbye and go back, because I was really worried about Peixin's condition. Unexpectedly, the table I joined was full of heavy drinkers. Although I held on to the principle of not fighting, my defense line was not strong and was finally breached by them. After several rounds of toasts, my alcohol tolerance had reached its limit. Because of past experiences, I did not want to step into drunkenness again, so I thought that outsmarting was better than fighting hard, so I slipped away quietly.

That night, the moon was bright and the stars were sparse. The warm southern wind blowing on my face was quite soothing. When I left, since I was sneaking away, I did not formally say goodbye, and Peixian did not see me off. At that time, the women's table had dispersed, but most of the dozen or so tables of male guests in the hall were still happily playing finger-guessing games. I also glanced at my neighboring table. My old friend Hawthorne was also nowhere to be seen. I knew that he often avoided ordinary social engagements. But this time, he actually came to celebrate in person because of my relationship with me. But since he had left before the end of the banquet, it could be seen that he also felt as impatient as I did.

I left the gate and walked slowly along the sidewalk on Huanghe Road. After those bursts of night wind, the heat on my face was indeed slightly reduced, but I still felt dizzy in my head, so I decided to walk back to exercise and allow the blood in my brain to circulate and descend. I walked to the corner of Huanghe Road and turned left into Qinghai Road. The carriages and horses that had been lined up there had all left, and there were no pedestrians to be seen. With one turn, one went from noise to quiet, and the scene changed. I couldn't help but think about the fate of life and the warmth and coldness of human relationships. There is only a difference of one turn. If Peixian's military position were to fall one day, then at the second celebration, the carriages and horses in front of the door would probably no longer be so crowded and lively.
